## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (mechanical vibrations / nonlinear oscillators)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form for (non)linear harmonic oscillators with restoring forces, damping, and external/parametric forcing. Common models include Duffing- and van der Pol-type oscillators and pendulum-like sinusoidal restoring forces.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (small-amplitude conservative oscillator; sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (mass-normalized spring-damper dynamics)
- Linear forcing (additive drive): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (harmonic external forcing)
- Duffing (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity, no damping)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (nonlinear spring + linear dissipation)
- Higher-order stiffness nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (strongly nonlinear restoring force expansion)
- Pendulum/sinusoidal restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (large-angle pendulum-like restoring, with damping)
- van der Pol oscillator (nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations / limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (self-excitation based on velocity)
- Quadratic/turbulent drag damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (nonlinear dissipation increasing with speed)
- Dry (Coulomb) friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (velocity-sign-like friction smoothed near v=0)
- Parametric excitation: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / Mathieu-type behavior)
- Nonlinear forced oscillator with harmonics: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) + c5 * sin(c4 * t) (general periodic drive with phase)
- State-dependent frequency (amplitude-dependent stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * x**2) * x + c2 * v (effective omega(x) behavior via cubic term factored)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope тЖТ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects тЖТ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay тЖТ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior тЖТ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects тЖТ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces are typically odd in x (e.g., x, x**3, sin(c*x)); this yields symmetric oscillations around x=0 when no forcing biases the system.
- Linear dissipation appears as a term proportional to v; it reduces amplitude over time and shifts resonance peaks under forcing.
- Self-excited oscillations/limit cycles are often modeled by damping that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c - x**2)*v (van der Pol) or (c - v**2)*v (Rayleigh).
- Hardening/softening behavior (frequency increasing/decreasing with amplitude) is captured by adding x**3 (and higher odd powers) to the restoring term.
- Large-angle geometric nonlinearities often replace x with sin(c*x) in the restoring force, producing amplitude-dependent period without polynomial divergence.
- External periodic forcing introduces explicit t dependence via sin(c*t) and cos(c*t); combinations allow arbitrary phase and multiple harmonics.
- Parametric resonance is suggested by stiffness terms multiplied by cos(c*t) (time-periodic coefficients on x), leading to Mathieu-like instability tongues.
- Nonlinear drag/friction is indicated by v*Abs(v) (quadratic drag) or tanh(c*v)/sign-like terms (Coulomb friction), producing amplitude decay that depends on speed rather than purely linearly.
- If dv_dt contains only x (and not t explicitly), the system is likely autonomous; explicit t terms imply driven or parametrically modulated dynamics.

GT: -mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x**c5
Candidate formulas: 73

GT (fully expanded):
\[
-0.431673711555058\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;1.47162300874852\,x^3\;-\;1.47162300874852\,x(0.0306959168053925\,t+1)
\]
Expand into monomials:
- \(v\) term: \(-0.431673711555058\,v\)
- \(v x^2\) term: \(+0.431673711555058\,v x^2\)
- \(x^3\) term: \(-1.47162300874852\,x^3\)
- \(x\) term: \(-1.47162300874852\,x\)
- \(t x\) term: \(-1.47162300874852\cdot 0.0306959168053925\, t x = -0.0451732357621442\, t x\)

So GT is exactly a linear combination of \(\{x,\;v,\;v x^2,\;x^3,\;t x\}\) with fixed coefficients, and **no other functional forms** (no denominators, logs, trig, exp, extra constants, etc.).

Below, a candidate can match iff we can set its free constants so that:
- it contains at least these five basis terms (or can reduce to them), and
- all extra terms can be eliminated by setting their coefficients to 0 (or otherwise made identically 0 for all \(x,t,v\), which is generally impossible for nontrivial functions like \(1/(c7 v+c8)\), \(\log(\cdot)\), \(\sin(\cdot)\), etc.).
